How does histone methylation affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone methylation: H3K4me3 active promoters, H3K36me3 active gene bodies, H3K27me3 repressed (Polycomb), H3K9me3 heterochromatin. Writers (SET domain), erasers (JMJD, LSD1), readers (chromodomains).
What is a synteny for polyploid crop breeding? | research | Polyploid crop breeding: synteny between subgenomes in wheat, cotton, strawberry guides selection, gene editing. Homeologous recombination, chromosome engineering for trait introgression.
Explain how Rho-dependent termination works | processes | Rho-dependent termination: Rho helicase binds rut site on RNA, translocates 5'→3', catches up to polymerase, unwinds RNA-DNA hybrid, releases transcript. Requires ATP.
What is a genetic marker for invasive species? | applications | Invasive species genetics: identify source populations, track spread, detect hybrids. SNPs for population structure, adaptive loci for local adaptation. Inform management strategies.
How does associative overdominance maintain variation? | evolution | Associative overdominance: deleterious recessive mutation appears overdominant because linked to beneficial variant. Maintains both alleles, increases neutral variation near selected site.
What is a ribozyme for RNA imaging? | research | RNA imaging with ribozymes: self-cleaving ribozymes generate defined ends for FISH probes; ribozyme-based reporters cleave to release fluorescent signal. For tracking RNA in live cells.
Explain how imprinting affects growth syndromes | disorders | Imprinting growth disorders: Beckwith-Wiedemann (overgrowth, paternal UPD/ methylation loss at 11p15), Silver-Russell (growth retardation, maternal UPD/ methylation gain). Opposite phenotypes from same chromosomal region.
What is a haplotype for complex trait prediction? | genetics | Haplotype-based prediction: use phased haplotypes in genomic prediction models, capture cis-interactions, improve accuracy over SNP-based methods for traits with epistasis.
How does CRISPR prime editing correct mutations? | technology | Prime editing corrects mutations without double-strand breaks: pegRNA guides nicked strand, reverse transcriptase writes correction, cellular repair incorporates. For Duchenne muscular dystrophy, Tay-Sachs in cells.
What is a genetic algorithm for architectural design? | applications | Evolutionary architecture: generate building designs optimizing energy efficiency, structural integrity, aesthetics. Encode parameters, evaluate with simulations, evolve innovative solutions.
Explain how Hox genes regulate apoptosis | genetics | Hox genes regulate apoptosis during development: sculpting digits (interdigital cell death), neural development. Dysregulation in cancer affects cell survival. Context-dependent pro- or anti-apoptotic.
What is a protoplast for secretion studies? | research | Protoplasts study protein secretion: collect apoplastic fluid easily, assay secreted proteins, study secretory pathway inhibitors. Plant systems for pharmaceutical protein production.
How does parental origin effect evolve? | evolution | Parental origin effects evolve through conflict: paternal genes in offspring benefit from extracting more resources from mother, maternal genes benefit from conserving resources for future offspring.
What is a genetic correlation with fertility? | research | Fertility genetics: age at first child, number of children have genetic component, correlates with education, health traits. Evolutionary implications: natural selection on modern traits.
Explain how virus vector vaccines work | technology | Viral vector vaccines: adenovirus, vesicular stomatitis virus engineered to express antigen. Replicating or non-replicating. Strong T cell responses. Ebola, COVID-19 vaccines. Preexisting immunity concern.
What is a morphogen in angiogenesis? | genetics | Angiogenesis morphogens: VEGF gradient attracts endothelial tip cells; Notch-Delta lateral inhibition specifies tip vs stalk cells; BMP, Wnt regulate vessel patterning. Therapeutic for ischemic disease.
How does single-cell multiome reveal regulation? | technology | Single-cell multiome (ATAC + RNA): link chromatin accessibility to gene expression in same cell. Identify regulatory elements driving expression, infer gene regulatory networks, study differentiation trajectories.
What is a genetic network for stress response? | research | Stress response networks: heat shock (HSF), oxidative stress (Nrf2), hypoxia (HIF), DNA damage (p53). Cross-talk, trade-offs. Engineering stress tolerance in crops, industrial microbes.
Explain how ring species demonstrate speciation | evolution | Ring species: connected chain of populations around barrier, adjacent populations interbreed, but ends where chain meets are reproductively isolated. Example: Ensatina salamanders around Central Valley.
What is a temperature-sensitive mutant for gene function? | research | Temperature-sensitive mutants: protein functional at permissive temperature, misfolds/nonfunctional at restrictive temperature. Acute loss-of-function, reversible. Classic in yeast, Drosophila, C. elegans.
How does transcription factor cooperativity work? | genetics | Transcription factor cooperativity: direct interaction, DNA bending, simultaneous binding to composite elements, cofactor recruitment. Creates specificity, sharp thresholds, combinatorial regulation.
What is a genetic switch for biodegradation timing? | engineering | Biodegradation timing switches: sense nutrient depletion, switch from growth to production phase; delay pathway expression until population size sufficient. Optimize yield in bioreactors.
Explain how morphological clocks estimate divergence | evolution | Morphological clocks: model morphological character evolution with Markov models, estimate divergence times from morphology alone. Less precise than molecular but useful for fossil-rich groups.
What is a human-rat chimera for disease modeling? | research | Human-rat chimeras: larger than mice, better for some physiology, behavior studies. Human hepatocytes in rat liver for drug metabolism; neural chimeras for Parkinson's. Lower contribution than mice.
How does RNA methylation affect translation? | epigenetics | m6A methylation affects translation: readers YTHDF1 promotes, YTHDF2 degrades mRNA, YTHDF3 ambiguous. Context-dependent, dynamic during stress, development. Links epitranscriptome to proteome.
What is a synteny for genome annotation in non-models? | research | Non-model genome annotation: transfer from model species using synteny, especially for gene-poor regions, non-coding elements. Improves functional inference where experimental data lacking.
Explain how promoter escape transitions to elongation | processes | Promoter escape: Pol II transitions from initiated complex to elongating complex, involves TFIIH phosphorylation of Pol II CTD, loss of some initiation factors, gain of elongation factors.
What is a genetic marker for conservation breeding? | applications | Conservation breeding markers: manage genetic diversity, minimize inbreeding, select breeding pairs. Pedigree reconstruction, kinship estimation, genome-wide metrics for small populations.
How does linked selection affect genome diversity? | evolution | Linked selection: selective sweeps and background selection reduce diversity at linked neutral sites. Creates heterogeneity in diversity along genome, correlation with recombination rate.
What is a ribozyme for RNA processing in synthetic circuits? | engineering | Synthetic ribozymes: self-cleaving ribozymes insulate genetic parts, prevent interference; ribozyme switches regulated by small molecules. Modular RNA parts for predictable circuit behavior.
Explain how imprinting affects mental health | disorders | Imprinting disorders affect mental health: Angelman (happy demeanor, severe ID), Prader-Willi (hyperphagia, OCD, psychosis risk). Parent-of-origin effects on brain development, behavior.
What is a haplotype for imputation in admixed populations? | genetics | Admixed population imputation: need reference panels including ancestral populations, account for local ancestry. Methods: RFMix, LAMP. Improves accuracy in underrepresented groups.
How does CRISPR screen identify host factors for viruses? | research | CRISPR screen for virus host factors: infect knockout library with virus, survivors lack essential host factors. Identified SARS-CoV-2 receptors, entry factors, antiviral pathways.
What is a genetic algorithm for vehicle routing? | applications | Vehicle routing with genetic algorithms: optimize delivery routes minimizing distance, time, vehicles. Encode routes, evaluate constraints, evolve efficient solutions for logistics companies.
Explain how Hox genes are regulated by retinoic acid | genetics | Retinoic acid regulates Hox genes: gradients established by synthesis/degradation enzymes, binds RAR/RXR receptors, activates 3' Hox genes first, posteriorizing effect. Used in developmental studies.
What is a protoplast for abiotic stress studies? | research | Protoplasts for abiotic stress: apply stressors (salt, drought, heat) uniformly, assay rapid responses (calcium signaling, ROS, gene expression). High-throughput screening for stress tolerance.
How does genomic imprinting affect complex traits? | genetics | Imprinting contributes to complex traits: height, birth weight, metabolic traits. Parent-of-origin effects detected in GWAS when parental genotypes available. Often tissue-specific.
What is a genetic correlation with sleep patterns? | research | Sleep genetics: duration, chronotype (morningness), disorders (insomnia, narcolepsy) heritable. Correlates with psychiatric, metabolic traits. CLOCK genes, but many loci with small effects.
Explain how adjuvants enhance vaccine response | technology | Adjuvants enhance vaccine immunity: aluminum salts (depot effect, inflammation), MF59 (oil-in-water emulsion), AS01 (MPL + QS-21). Activate innate immunity, improve antigen presentation.
What is a morphogen in tooth development? | genetics | Tooth development morphogens: BMP4 initiates tooth formation; FGF, SHH, Wnt regulate bud, cap, bell stages; gradients determine cusp patterning. Used in regenerative dentistry.
How does spatial transcriptomics map disease lesions? | technology | Spatial transcriptomics in disease: map gene expression in tumor microenvironment, plaque in atherosclerosis, lesions in multiple sclerosis. Identify cell interactions, spatial gradients of pathology.
What is a genetic network for apoptosis? | research | Apoptosis network: intrinsic (mitochondrial) and extrinsic (death receptor) pathways, caspase cascade, Bcl-2 family regulation. Cross-talk with survival pathways, disrupted in cancer.
Explain how parapatric speciation occurs | evolution | Parapatric speciation: divergence with limited gene flow along environmental gradient. Selection differential across gradient leads to adaptation, reproductive isolation. Example: heavy metal tolerance in plants.
What is a optogenetic CRISPR for neuronal editing? | research | Optogenetic CRISPR: light-activated Cas9 for precise neuronal genome editing. Combine with neuronal activity markers to edit active neurons. Study memory, circuit function.
How does translesion synthesis bypass damage? | processes | Translesion synthesis: specialized DNA polymerases (Pol ζ, η, ι, κ) replicate past lesions with low fidelity, error-prone but allows survival. Regulated by PCNA ubiquitination.
What is a genetic switch for population synchronization? | engineering | Population synchronization: quorum sensing coupled to gene expression, synchronizes behavior across population. Applications: coordinated lysis, biofilm formation, oscillatory dynamics.
Explain how tip calibration improves molecular dating | evolution | Tip calibration: use radiocarbon dates or historical samples as tip dates in Bayesian phylogenetics. For recent evolution (viruses, domesticates), very precise rates.
What is a human-cow chimera for agriculture? | research | Human-cow chimeras theoretically for organ farming, but ethical concerns greater due to emotional connection. Not pursued seriously; focus on pigs, sheep.
How does histone acetylation activate genes? | epigenetics | Histone acetylation neutralizes lysine charge, weakens histone-DNA interaction, opens chromatin. Readers (bromodomains) recruit transcription machinery. Writers (HATs), erasers (HDACs).
What is a synteny for translational research? | research | Translational research synteny: mouse-human synteny identifies orthologous regions for disease gene mapping. Mouse models for human disorders, drug testing. >90% of human genes have mouse orthologs.
Explain how intrinsic termination hairpins form | processes | Intrinsic termination hairpin: GC-rich stem stabilizes, loop of 4-8 nt, followed by 7-9 U residues. RNA polymerase pauses at hairpin, U-rich region weakens hybrid, transcript releases.
What is a genetic marker for fishery management? | applications | Fishery genetics: stock identification (microsatellites, SNPs), mixed stock analysis, illegal fishing detection. Manage sustainable harvest, protect endangered populations.
How does Hill-Robertson interference affect evolution? | evolution | Hill-Robertson interference: selection at one locus reduces effective population size for linked loci, reducing efficacy of selection. Increases background selection, reduces diversity.
What is a ribozyme for RNA therapeutics delivery? | applications | Ribozyme-based therapeutics: self-cleaving ribozymes release therapeutic RNA (siRNA, aptamer) from carrier transcript. Improve stability, control release. In development.
Explain how imprinting affects metabolism | disorders | Imprinting affects metabolism: Prader-Willi hyperphagia, obesity; Temple syndrome (maternal UPD14) insulin resistance; transient neonatal diabetes (paternal UPD6). Imprinted genes in hypothalamic feeding centers.
What is a haplotype for precision medicine? | genetics | Precision medicine haplotypes: HLA haplotypes for drug hypersensitivity (abacavir); CYP450 haplotypes for metabolism; warfarin dosing haplotypes (VKORC1, CYP2C9). Guide personalized treatment.
How does CRISPR identify non-coding functions? | research | CRISPR screens of non-coding regions: tiling guides across enhancers, promoters, identify regulatory elements. Couple with single-cell RNA-seq (Perturb-seq) for high-resolution mapping.
What is a genetic algorithm for stock trading? | applications | Algorithmic trading with genetic algorithms: evolve trading strategies, technical indicators. Evaluate on historical data, optimize profit, risk management. Adaptive to market changes.
Explain how Hox genes are repressed by Polycomb | genetics | Polycomb represses Hox genes: PRC2 deposits H3K27me3, PRC1 compact chromatin. Maintains silenced state after initial repression. Essential for proper Hox expression patterns, memory.
What is a protoplast for pathogen interaction studies? | research | Protoplast-pathogen interactions: study early signaling, oxidative burst, defense gene activation. Synchronous system, but missing cell wall components important for recognition.
How does parent-of-origin effect manifest in GWAS? | genetics | Parent-of-origin GWAS: need trio data to assign alleles to parents. Detect imprinting effects, maternal genotype effects (through intrauterine environment). Complex study design.
What is a genetic correlation with personality? | research | Personality genetics: Big Five traits heritable (~40-60%), correlate with psychiatric disorders, cognitive abilities. Polygenic scores predict some variance, gene-environment interactions important.
Explain how mRNA vaccine storage improved | technology | mRNA vaccine storage stability: lipid nanoparticle formulations, buffer optimization, freeze-drying. COVID-19 vaccines now stable at refrigerator temperatures for months, improving distribution.
What is a morphogen in hair follicle cycling? | genetics | Hair follicle cycling morphogens: Wnt activates growth (anagen), BMP promotes regression (catagen), FGF maintains quiescence (telogen). Dermal papilla signals regulate stem cell activation.
How does single-cell epigenomics reveal cell states? | technology | Single-cell epigenomics defines cell states: chromatin accessibility landscapes identify regulatory programs, trajectory inference, rare cell types. Complement to transcriptomics for identity.
What is a genetic network for cell cycle? | research | Cell cycle network: cyclin-CDK complexes, checkpoint controls (p53, RB), ubiquitin ligases (APC/C, SCF). Oscillatory dynamics, ensures ordered progression, disrupted in cancer.
Explain how speciation with gene flow occurs | evolution | Speciation with gene flow: divergent selection overcome gene flow, facilitated by reduced recombination (inversions, islands of divergence). Genomic islands of speciation, porous species boundaries.
What is a chemical-inducible dimerization for control? | research | Chemical-inducible dimerization: FKBP-FRB with rapamycin; ABA-PYL with abscisic acid. Recruit proteins to specific locations, control activity. For signaling reconstruction, optogenetics alternative.
How does transcription factor pioneer activity work? | genetics | Pioneer factors (FoxA, Oct4) bind closed chromatin, initiate opening, allow other factors access. Involved in reprogramming, development. Recognize DNA in nucleosomes, recruit remodelers.
What is a genetic switch for metabolic burden control? | engineering | Metabolic burden control: sense cellular resources (ATP, ribosomes), downregulate expression if burden high. Dynamic regulation optimizes production without growth inhibition.
Explain how fossil age uncertainty affects dating | evolution | Fossil age uncertainty: radiometric dating errors, stratigraphic uncertainty. Bayesian methods incorporate uncertainty as prior distributions. Multiple fossils per node reduce overall error.
What is a human-nonhuman primate chimera ethics? | research | Human-nonhuman primate chimera ethics: concern about human cells in brain (consciousness), germline. Guidelines: limit contribution, monitor, no breeding. Scientific value vs ethical boundaries.
How does RNA modification affect viral replication? | epigenetics | Viral RNA modifications: host m6A machinery modifies viral RNA, affecting stability, translation, immune recognition. Viruses hijack or evade. Antiviral target?
What is a synteny for crop wild relative utilization? | research | Crop wild relatives: synteny guides introgression of valuable traits (disease resistance, stress tolerance) from wild to cultivated species. Pre-breeding for climate resilience.
Explain how abortive cycling regulates initiation | processes | Abortive cycling: Pol II synthesizes short RNAs without promoter escape, may clear promoter, regulate timing. Transition to productive elongation involves overcoming barrier, possibly NELF dissociation.
What is a genetic marker for rewilding projects? | applications | Rewilding genetics: source appropriate genotypes for reintroduction, maintain adaptive variation, avoid outbreeding depression. Genomic assessment of founder populations.
How does soft sweep affect adaptation? | evolution | Soft sweep: adaptation from standing variation or multiple mutations, leaves different signature than hard sweep (single new mutation). More common in natural populations, harder to detect.
What is a ribozyme for RNA assembly? | engineering | Ribozyme for RNA assembly: self-splicing introns ligate exons, used to assemble multiple RNA parts into long constructs. Synthetic biology for large RNA synthesis.
Explain how imprinting affects social behavior | genetics | Imprinted genes affect social behavior: Peg3 maternal care, Grb10 dominance, Ube3a social engagement. Possibly evolved in context of kin conflict, parental investment.
What is a haplotype for organ transplant matching? | genetics | Transplant matching: HLA haplotypes, also minor histocompatibility antigens, KIR haplotypes. Haploidentical transplants with post-transplant cyclophosphamide allow mismatched donors.
How does CRISPR activation screen for enhancers? | research | CRISPRa screen for enhancers: dCas9-activator tiling across regulatory regions, measure gene activation. Identify functional enhancers, validate disease-associated non-coding variants.
What is a genetic algorithm for network design? | applications | Network design with genetic algorithms: optimize topology, routing, capacity of communication, transport networks. Evolve resilient, efficient networks under constraints.
Explain how Hox genes are involved in regeneration | genetics | Hox genes re-expressed during regeneration: position identity memory, pattern blastema. In axolotl limb regeneration, HoxA13-D13 expressed in distal blastema, recapitulating development.
What is a protoplast for genome-wide association? | research | Protoplast GWAS: assay cellular traits (ion flux, stress response) across diverse genotypes, link to genomics. High-throughput phenotyping for cell biology traits.
How does parent-of-origin effect evolve in plants? | evolution | Plant imprinting: fewer genes, different evolutionary forces? Some evidence for parental conflict in endosperm. Convergent evolution with mammals for seed development.
What is a genetic correlation with exercise response? | research | Exercise response genetics: VO2 max improvement, muscle strength, injury risk heritable. Correlates with health outcomes. Personalized exercise prescriptions based on genetics?
Explain how vaccine platforms compare | technology | Vaccine platforms: mRNA (rapid development, strong immunity), viral vector (strong T cells), protein subunit (safety, weaker immunity), whole inactivated (traditional). Platform choice depends on pathogen.
What is a morphogen in bone healing? | genetics | Bone healing morphogens: BMPs induce osteogenesis, TGF-β, FGF, Wnt regulate. Used clinically (BMP-2) for spinal fusion, non-union fractures. Delivery challenges: concentration, localization.
How does spatial multi-omics integrate data? | technology | Spatial multi-omics integration: align transcriptomic, proteomic, metabolomic layers using image registration, joint dimensionality reduction. Understand tissue organization, cell-cell communication.
What is a genetic network for neurodevelopment? | research | Neurodevelopment network: transcription factors (Pax6, Neurog2), signaling (Notch, Shh), cell adhesion. Disrupted in autism, intellectual disability. Organoid models for testing.
Explain how peripatric speciation occurs | evolution | Peripatric speciation: small isolated population at edge of range undergoes rapid divergence due to founder effect, genetic drift, selection. May involve genetic revolution.
What is a optogenetic transcription factor? | research | Optogenetic transcription factors: light-sensitive DNA-binding domains (LOV, CRY2) fused to activators/repressors. Control gene expression with light patterns, precise spatial-temporal.
How does homologous recombination repair DSBs? | processes | Homologous recombination: resect DSB ends, Rad51 filament invades homologous template, DNA synthesis, resolve intermediates. Error-free, uses sister chromatid template. Essential in meiosis.
What is a genetic switch for containment in GMOs? | engineering | GMO containment: suicide switches (kill upon escape), auxotrophy, dependency on synthetic amino acid. Biocontainment for environmental release of engineered organisms.
Explain how molecular clocks account for rate variation | evolution | Relaxed clock models: uncorrelated (rates independent across branches), autocorrelated (rates similar in adjacent branches). Bayesian inference with MCMC samples from posterior distribution.
What is a human-pig chimera for diabetes research? | research | Human-pig chimeras with pancreatic human cells could model diabetes, test therapies. Challenges: low contribution, immune rejection, ethical concerns about chimeric animals.
How does histone phosphorylation affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone phosphorylation: H3S10ph during mitosis, transcription activation; H2AXph in DNA damage. Kinases (Aurora B, ATM), phosphatases. Rapid, dynamic signaling.
What is a synteny for vertebrate evolution studies? | research | Vertebrate evolution synteny: conserved blocks across mammals, more rearrangements in fish, amphibians. Whole genome duplications in vertebrate ancestor, teleost fish.
Explain how Rho protein terminates transcription | processes | Rho: hexameric RNA helicase, binds rut site (C-rich, unstructured), translocates 5'→3' using ATP, catches polymerase, unwinds hybrid. Requires Rho utilization sites on transcript.
What is a genetic marker for climate adaptation? | applications | Climate adaptation genetics: identify alleles associated with climate variables (temperature, precipitation) across populations. Genomic prediction for assisted migration, breeding.
How does associative overdominance maintain polymorphisms? | evolution | Associative overdominance: deleterious allele maintained because linked to beneficial allele in repulsion phase. Appears as overdominance at locus, maintains both alleles.
What is a ribozyme for RNA detection? | applications | Ribozyme-based biosensors: allosteric ribozymes activated by binding small molecule, cleave reporter RNA. For detection of metabolites, toxins, pathogens. Field-deployable.
Explain how imprinting affects cardiovascular disease | disorders | Imprinting and CVD: some loci show parent-of-origin effects on blood pressure, lipid levels. PEG3, DLK1 implicated. Epigenetic mechanisms may mediate fetal programming of adult disease.
What is a haplotype for pharmacogenomics dosing? | genetics | Pharmacogenomics haplotypes: CYP2D6 metabolizer status (poor, intermediate, extensive, ultrarapid) based on haplotype; TPMT for thiopurines; DPYD for fluoropyrimidines. Clinical implementation.
How does CRISPRi screen for essential genes? | research | CRISPRi screen: dCas9-KRAB represses transcription, partial knockdown, less severe than knockout. Identify essential genes without killing cells, study dosage sensitivity.
What is a genetic algorithm for robot control? | applications | Evolutionary robotics: evolve neural controllers for walking, grasping, navigation. Transfer from simulation to physical robots, adapt to damage, novel environments.
Explain how Hox genes specify regional identity | genetics | Hox code specifies regional identity along axis: cervical, thoracic, lumbar vertebrae identity; limb position. Misexpression changes identity (thoracic to cervical vertebrae in mice).
What is a protoplast for synthetic biology? | research | Protoplasts for synthetic biology: introduce synthetic circuits, test in plant context without stable transformation. Rapid prototyping, characterize parts, optimize before stable transformation.
How does genomic imprinting affect IVF outcomes? | genetics | IVF may affect imprinting: culture conditions, hormonal stimulation linked to imprinting disorders (Beckwith-Wiedemann, Angelman slightly increased). Epigenetic risks under study.
What is a genetic correlation with intelligence? | research | Intelligence genetics: highly polygenic, ~50% heritability, correlates with education, health outcomes. Gene-environment interplay: genetic effects magnified in enriched environments.
Explain how viral vector vaccines are designed | technology | Viral vector design: delete essential genes (E1 in adenovirus), insert antigen gene, often with stronger promoter. Replication-incompetent, produced in complementing cell lines.
What is a morphogen in liver zonation? | genetics | Liver zonation morphogens: Wnt/β-catenin gradient from central vein creates metabolic zones (periportal vs perivenous). Ammonia detoxification, drug metabolism vary across lobule.
How does single-cell TCR/BCR sequencing work? | technology | Single-cell immune sequencing: capture TCR/BCR with transcriptome, pair chains, analyze clonality, antigen specificity. For vaccine response, autoimmunity, cancer immunology.
What is a genetic network for photosynthesis? | research | Photosynthesis network: light harvesting, electron transport, Calvin cycle genes co-regulated. Engineering for improved efficiency, C4 pathway into C3 plants. Synthetic chloroplasts.
Explain how reinforcement strengthens isolation | evolution | Reinforcement: selection against hybrids favors assortative mating alleles. Can complete speciation in sympatry, may leave genomic signature of elevated divergence in mating loci.
What is a temperature-sensitive allele for development? | research | Temperature-sensitive alleles: study essential genes by shifting temperature at different stages. Determine critical periods, analyze sequence of events in development.
How does transcription factor concentration matter? | genetics | Transcription factor concentration effects: gradients activate different targets at different thresholds; ultrasensitive responses from cooperativity; noise filtering from binding kinetics.
What is a genetic switch for production phase control? | engineering | Two-phase fermentation: growth phase then production phase switched by nutrient depletion, population density, or inducer. Maximize biomass then redirect metabolism to product.
Explain how total evidence dating handles fossils | evolution | Total evidence dating: morphological and molecular data in same likelihood model, fossils as tips with dates. All data inform topology and dates, better than separate analyses.
What is a human-mouse neural chimera for disease? | research | Human neurons in mouse brain model Alzheimer's, Parkinson's, autism. Study human-specific aspects, test drugs. Limitations: mouse environment, lack of human glia, circuit integration.
How does m6A affect RNA stability? | epigenetics | m6A affects stability: YTHDF2 recruits decay machinery; also affects translation efficiency, splicing. Dynamic during stress, development. Writers (METTL3/14), erasers (FTO, ALKBH5).
What is a synteny for gene family evolution? | research | Gene family evolution: synteny reveals duplication events (tandem, segmental, whole genome), subsequent divergence, neofunctionalization. Birth-death evolution of multigene families.
Explain how promoter clearance occurs | processes | Promoter clearance: Pol II escapes promoter, loses some initiation factors (TFIIB, TFIIE), gains elongation factors (TFIIS, P-TEFb). Transition marked by CTD phosphorylation pattern change.
What is a genetic marker for de-extinction? | applications | De-extinction genetics: compare ancient DNA to closest living relatives, identify key differences, use CRISPR to edit. Example: mammoth traits in elephant. Ethical, ecological considerations.
How does background selection shape genomes? | evolution | Background selection reduces diversity near genes, more in low recombination regions. Creates correlation between gene density and diversity. Important for interpreting genomic landscapes.
What is a ribozyme for RNA nanotechnology? | engineering | RNA nanotechnology: ribozymes for precise cleavage to generate RNA nanostructures with defined ends. Self-assembling RNA tiles, origami. Drug delivery, sensors.
Explain how imprinting affects brain imprinting | disorders | Brain-specific imprinting: some genes imprinted only in brain, not other tissues. Example: INPP5F neuron-specific imprinting. May affect neurodevelopmental disorders, behavior.
What is a haplotype for ancestry-specific risk? | genetics | Ancestry-specific risk haplotypes: some disease-associated haplotypes differ in frequency across populations, affecting risk differences. Important for equitable genomic medicine.
How does CRISPR screen identify synthetic lethals? | research | Synthetic lethal screen: knockout library in cancer cell line with oncogenic mutation, identify genes essential only in mutant background. Therapeutic targets (PARP in BRCA).
What is a genetic algorithm for antenna design? | applications | Evolutionary antenna design: NASA evolved satellite antenna with unusual shape, optimal performance. Encode shape parameters, evaluate with electromagnetic simulation, evolve.
Explain how Hox genes are regulated by miRNAs | genetics | miRNAs regulate Hox genes: miR-196 targets HoxB8, HoxC8, HoxD8; miR-10 targets HoxB3, HoxD10. Fine-tune expression, sharpen boundaries. Conserved across species.
What is a protoplast for CRISPR delivery? | research | Protoplast CRISPR: deliver RNP complexes by PEG or electroporation, high efficiency, no DNA integration. Regenerate edited plants. Transient expression avoids off-target integration.
How does parent-of-origin effect affect complex diseases? | genetics | Parent-of-origin effects in complex diseases: type 2 diabetes, autoimmune diseases show some imprinted loci. May explain missing heritability, family history patterns.
What is a genetic correlation with aging biomarkers? | research | Aging biomarkers genetics: telomere length, epigenetic clocks (DNA methylation age), senescence markers heritable. Correlate with lifespan, age-related diseases. Interventions to slow aging.
Explain how adjuvant selection affects vaccines | technology | Adjuvant selection: match to pathogen and vaccine platform. TLR agonists for viral vaccines; alum for protein vaccines; emulsion for influenza. Tailor immune response (Th1 vs Th2).
What is a morphogen in kidney development? | genetics | Kidney development morphogens: GDNF from metanephric mesenchyme attracts ureteric bud; Wnt, FGF, BMP regulate branching, nephron formation. Used in organoid differentiation.
How does spatial transcriptomics guide therapy? | technology | Spatial transcriptomics in cancer: map tumor heterogeneity, identify resistant subclones, tumor-immune interactions. Guide biopsy, predict response, develop combination therapies.
What is a genetic network for fermentation? | research | Fermentation network: glycolytic genes co-regulated; redox balance (NAD/NADH); byproduct formation. Engineering for biofuel, chemical production. Dynamic control strategies.
Explain how magic traits facilitate speciation | evolution | Magic traits: traits under divergent selection also cause assortative mating. Example: coloration affects both camouflage and mate preference. Speciation with gene flow more likely.
What is a light-activated Cas9 for spatial control? | research | Light-activated Cas9: split Cas9 fragments fused to photo-dimerizable domains, reconstitute with light. Spatial control for developmental studies, minimize off-targets.
How does non-homologous end joining work? | processes | NHEJ: Ku binds DSB ends, Artemis processes, DNA-PKcs phosphorylates, XLF/XRCC4/Ligase IV ligates. Error-prone, often creates small indels. Major DSB repair pathway in G1.
What is a genetic switch for bioproduction optimization? | engineering | Dynamic pathway regulation: sense intermediate levels, feedback regulate enzyme expression to avoid toxicity, balance flux. Improve yield, titer, productivity in metabolic engineering.
Explain how tip dating uses ancient DNA | evolution | Tip dating with ancient DNA: include ancient samples as tips with radiocarbon dates, estimate evolutionary rates over short timescales. For pathogens, domesticates, recent evolution.
What is a human-monkey chimera for neuroscience? | research | Human-monkey brain chimeras: study human brain evolution, model neurological diseases. Highly controversial, major ethical concerns about consciousness. Not currently pursued.
How does histone ubiquitination affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone ubiquitination: H2Bub1 promotes H3K4me3, transcription activation; H2Aub repression. Writers (RNF20/40), erasers (USP22). Cross-talk with other modifications.
What is a synteny for polyploid evolution? | research | Polyploid evolution synteny: compare subgenomes to diploid progenitors, track fractionation (gene loss), neofunctionalization. Allopolyploid vs autopolyploid patterns. Adaptive significance.
Explain how intrinsic termination efficiency varies | processes | Intrinsic termination efficiency depends on hairpin stability (GC pairs, length), U-stretch length, spacing between them. Engineered terminators for synthetic biology.
What is a genetic marker for sustainable forestry? | applications | Forestry genetics: growth rate, wood quality, pest resistance markers. Genomic selection for breeding, clonal propagation. Sustainable management, climate resilience.
How does hitchhiking affect neutral variation? | evolution | Genetic hitchhiking: selective sweep carries linked neutral alleles to fixation, reducing diversity. Signature: reduced diversity, skewed site frequency spectrum near selected site.
What is a ribozyme for RNA assembly in vitro? | research | In vitro RNA assembly: ribozymes ligate RNA fragments, used to synthesize long RNAs for structural studies, therapeutics. RNA synthesis without protein enzymes.
Explain how imprinting affects placental function | disorders | Imprinted genes crucial for placental function: transport (Igf2), hormone production, invasion. Dysregulation in preeclampsia, intrauterine growth restriction. Mouse models elucidate.
What is a haplotype for immunotherapy response? | genetics | Immunotherapy response: HLA haplotypes affect neoantigen presentation; immune gene haplotypes (PD-1, CTLA-4) influence checkpoint inhibitor response. Biomarkers for cancer immunotherapy.
How does CRISPR screen identify enhancer-gene links? | research | CRISPRi/a tiling across enhancers with single-cell RNA-seq (Perturb-seq) maps enhancer-gene connections at scale. Systems genetics for non-coding genome.
What is a genetic algorithm for music style imitation? | applications | Music style imitation: evolve compositions in style of Bach, Beatles, etc. Fitness based on similarity to training corpus. Generate new music in desired style.
Explain how Hox genes affect cell migration | genetics | Hox genes regulate cell migration: in neural crest, hematopoietic stem cells, cancer metastasis. Control adhesion molecules, chemokine receptors. Context-dependent effects.
What is a protoplast for organelle editing? | research | Organelle editing: deliver CRISPR to protoplasts for mitochondrial or chloroplast genome editing. Challenging due to multiple copies, but progress with TALENs, CRISPR.
How does parent-of-origin effect evolve in marsupials? | evolution | Marsupial imprinting: fewer genes imprinted, different patterns? Study evolution of imprinting across mammalian lineages. Implications for conflict theory.
What is a genetic correlation with gut microbiome? | research | Host genetics influences gut microbiome composition (~10% heritable). Correlates with diet, metabolism, immune traits. Mendelian randomization to infer causality.
Explain how nanoparticle formulation affects vaccines | technology | Nanoparticle formulation: size affects lymph node drainage; surface charge affects cellular uptake; PEGylation reduces clearance. Optimize for antigen presentation, immune response.
What is a morphogen in lung development? | genetics | Lung development morphogens: FGF10 from mesenchyme promotes budding; SHH, BMP pattern branching; Wnt regulates proximal-distal differentiation. Used in lung organoids.
How does single-cell epigenomics define lineages? | technology | Single-cell epigenomics lineage tracing: chromatin accessibility patterns reconstruct developmental trajectories, identify branch points, regulatory changes driving fate decisions.
What is a genetic network for nitrogen fixation? | research | Nitrogen fixation network: nif genes in bacteria, regulation by oxygen, ammonia. Engineering into crops (cereals) for sustainable agriculture. Synthetic symbiosis.
Explain how chromosomal speciation occurs | evolution | Chromosomal speciation: rearrangements (fusions, fissions, inversions) reduce fertility in heterozygotes, lead to reproductive isolation. Can be primary cause or reinforce divergence.
What is a degron for rapid protein depletion? | research | Auxin-inducible degron (AID): fuse protein to AID tag, add auxin, recruits TIR1 E3 ligase, ubiquitination, proteasomal degradation. Minutes-scale depletion, reversible.
How does transcription factor mobility affect binding? | genetics | Transcription factor mobility: measured by FRAP, some rapidly exchange (seconds), others stable (minutes). Affects response dynamics, noise filtering, memory.
What is a genetic switch for minimal genome cells? | engineering | Minimal genome cells: essential genes under inducible control, study minimal requirements for life. Synthetic biology for chassis cells with designed regulation.
Explain how fossil preservation bias affects dating | evolution | Fossil preservation bias: hard parts fossilize better, terrestrial less than marine, recent better than ancient. Models account for incomplete sampling, but bias remains.
What is a human-pig chimera for xenotransplantation? | research | Xenotransplantation: genetically modify pigs to reduce rejection (delete α-Gal, add human complement regulators). Recent heart transplants to terminally ill patients.
How does RNA modification affect neurodegeneration? | epigenetics | RNA modification dysregulation in neurodegeneration: FTO m6A demethylase associated with Alzheimer's; TDP-43 affects RNA processing. Epitranscriptomic therapies potential.
What is a synteny for genome size evolution? | research | Genome size evolution: synteny shows expansions (transposon bursts) and contractions (deletions). Compare related species with different sizes (pufferfish vs other fish).
Explain how promoter-proximal pausing releases | processes | Pause release: P-TEFb phosphorylates NELF, DSIF, Pol II CTD; NELF dissociates, DSIF becomes positive factor; Pol II enters productive elongation. Regulated by signaling pathways.
What is a genetic marker for pollinator conservation? | applications | Pollinator genetics: population structure of bees, butterflies; pesticide resistance; climate adaptation. Inform conservation strategies, habitat corridors.
How does soft sweep appear in genomic data? | evolution | Soft sweep signature: multiple haplotypes carry selected allele, intermediate frequency haplotypes, less extreme reduction in diversity. Harder to distinguish from neutral.
What is a ribozyme for RNA replication? | research | Self-replicating ribozymes: RNA polymerase ribozymes that copy themselves, albeit slowly. Laboratory evolution improving efficiency. Origin of life research.
Explain how imprinting affects embryonic growth | disorders | Imprinting and embryonic growth: Igf2 promotes, Igf2r restricts; other imprinted genes affect placental function, nutrient transfer. Fetal programming of adult disease.
What is a haplotype for transplant tolerance? | genetics | Transplant tolerance: matching for non-inherited maternal antigens (NIMA) can induce tolerance; HLA haplotypes important. Mixed chimerism for tolerance induction.
How does CRISPR screen map genetic interactions? | research | Genetic interaction mapping: double CRISPR knockout library, measure fitness, identify synthetic lethal, suppressor interactions. Map epistasis networks, pathway relationships.
What is a genetic algorithm for protein design? | applications | Protein design with genetic algorithms: evolve amino acid sequences for desired structure, function. Rosetta design, but evolutionary approaches for novel folds.
Explain how Hox genes regulate differentiation | genetics | Hox genes regulate differentiation: control cell type-specific genes in different segments. Examples: motor neuron subtypes in spinal cord; keratinocyte differentiation in skin.
What is a protoplast for high-throughput screening? | research | High-throughput protoplast screening: 96/384-well formats, automated dispensing, fluorescence readouts. For drug discovery, gene function, synthetic biology parts characterization.
How does genomic imprinting affect behavior evolution? | evolution | Imprinting evolution for behavior: conflict over social behavior (altruism, aggression) between maternally and paternally inherited genes? Theoretical, limited evidence.
What is a genetic correlation with circadian rhythms? | research | Circadian rhythm genetics: morningness/eveningness, shift work tolerance, sleep disorders. Correlates with mental health, metabolism. CLOCK genes but many others.
Explain how vaccine platforms can be combined | technology | Heterologous prime-boost: prime with one platform (viral vector), boost with another (mRNA). Often stronger immune response. COVID-19 trials, HIV vaccine strategies.
What is a morphogen in retina development? | genetics | Retina development morphogens: SHH from ganglion cells patterns layers; FGF, BMP regulate cell fates. Used in retinal organoids for disease modeling, transplantation.
How does spatial transcriptomics map brain regions? | technology | Spatial transcriptomics maps brain regions: layer-specific gene expression in cortex, nuclei in hypothalamus, gradients in hippocampus. Brain atlases with molecular definition.
What is a genetic network for symbiosis? | research | Symbiosis network: legume-rhizobium Nod factor signaling; mycorrhizal symbiosis; coral-algae. Coevolution, recognition, nutrient exchange. Engineering novel symbioses.
Explain how ring species show speciation continuum | evolution | Ring species show speciation continuum: adjacent populations interbreed, ends do not. Demonstrates how geographic isolation can lead to speciation gradually. Classic example: Larus gulls.
What is a temperature-sensitive period for development? | research | Temperature-sensitive periods: apply heat shock at specific times to disrupt gene function temporally. Map critical windows for developmental processes.
How does transcription factor clustering affect genes? | genetics | Transcription factor clustering: hubs, phase separation create high local concentration, cooperative binding, super-enhancers. Regulates gene expression bursts, cell identity.
What is a genetic switch for timed expression? | engineering | Timed expression switches: delay circuits based on repressor degradation, feedforward loops. Program sequential gene expression for development, differentiation in synthetic biology.
Explain how molecular dating validates phylogenies | evolution | Molecular dating: consistent dates across genes suggest correct topology; conflicts may indicate incomplete lineage sorting, hybridization. Cross-validation with fossil dates.
What is a human-mouse chimera for blood disorders? | research | Human hematopoiesis in mouse: human stem cells in immunodeficient mice model blood cancers, test therapies. Humanized mouse models for immunology, infectious disease.
How does histone methylation memory work? | epigenetics | Histone methylation memory: H3K27me3 maintained through cell division by PRC2 reading existing marks, propagating. Epigenetic inheritance of gene expression states.
What is a synteny for disease gene discovery? | research | Disease gene discovery: synteny between human and model organism genomes identifies orthologs of disease genes. Mouse models for human diseases, drug testing.
Explain how Rho recognizes rut sites | processes | Rho recognizes rut sites: binds preferentially to C-rich, unstructured RNA. rut site typically 70-80 nt upstream of termination point. Mutations affect termination efficiency.
What is a genetic marker for coral reef restoration? | applications | Coral genetics: heat tolerance alleles, disease resistance, growth rate. Assisted evolution, selective breeding, larval seeding for reef restoration amid climate change.
How does associative overdominance affect load? | evolution | Associative overdominance reduces genetic load: maintains polymorphism without heterozygote advantage at locus itself. But load from linked deleterious alleles remains.
What is a ribozyme for RNA labeling in vivo? | research | In vivo RNA labeling: self-cleaving ribozymes produce ends for ligation of fluorescent tags. RNA imaging with click chemistry, fluorescence in situ hybridization.
Explain how imprinting affects mental illness risk | disorders | Imprinting and mental illness: Prader-Willi psychosis risk; some parent-of-origin effects in schizophrenia, bipolar disorder. Imprinted genes expressed in brain relevant to neuropsychiatry.
What is a haplotype for drug response prediction? | genetics | Polygenic haplotypes for drug response: combine multiple variants across genes in pathway. Better prediction than single SNPs for complex pharmacokinetics, pharmacodynamics.
How does CRISPR screen identify resistance mechanisms? | research | Resistance mechanism screens: treat cells with drug, select survivors, CRISPR screen identifies genes whose loss confers resistance. Guide combination therapies, understand resistance.
What is a genetic algorithm for circuit design? | applications | Electronic circuit design: evolve analog/digital circuits for specific functions. Unconventional solutions, optimize for size, power, speed. Hardware evolution.
Explain how Hox genes are involved in evolution of body plans | evolution | Hox gene changes underlie major body plan evolution: arthropod segment diversity; vertebrate axial patterning; loss of limbs in snakes. Regulatory changes key.
What is a protoplast for cell wall studies? | research | Cell wall studies: regenerate protoplasts, monitor wall deposition, composition. Study cell wall biosynthesis mutants, effects on morphology, defense.
How does parent-of-origin effect affect quantitative traits? | genetics | Quantitative trait parent-of-origin effects: detected in livestock, plants for growth, yield. Use in breeding: select based on parental origin of alleles.
What is a genetic correlation with educational mobility? | research | Educational mobility genetics: correlation between genetics for education and upward mobility. Gene-environment correlation: genetic factors influence environment exposure opportunities.
Explain how mRNA vaccine manufacturing scales | technology | mRNA vaccine manufacturing: in vitro transcription from DNA template, capping, purification, lipid nanoparticle formulation. Scalable, rapid, pandemic response capability.
What is a morphogen in pancreas development? | genetics | Pancreas development morphogens: FGF, BMP from notochord induce pancreas; SHH repression necessary; TGF-β, Notch regulate endocrine vs exocrine fate. Diabetes research.
How does single-cell multi-omics reveal plasticity? | technology | Cell plasticity: multi-omics captures intermediate states during transdifferentiation, dedifferentiation. Identify key regulators, epigenetic barriers to reprogramming.
What is a genetic network for stress signaling in plants? | research | Plant stress signaling: hormone pathways (ABA, JA, SA), transcription factors, ROS signaling. Engineering drought tolerance, pathogen resistance. Climate-resilient crops.
Explain how ecological speciation occurs | evolution | Ecological speciation: divergent selection based on ecological differences (diet, habitat) leads to reproductive isolation. Often involves adaptive traits, assortative mating.
What is a light-activated gene expression system? | research | Light-activated gene expression: LOV domains fused to transcription factors, dimerize with light. Precise spatial-temporal control for developmental biology, optogenetics.
How does microhomology-mediated end joining work? | processes | MMEJ: uses 5-25 bp microhomologies to join ends, involves Pol θ, Lig3, often deletional. More error-prone than NHEJ. Important in some cancers, genome editing outcomes.
What is a genetic switch for metabolic pathway balancing? | engineering | Metabolic pathway balancing: sense intermediate accumulation, dynamically adjust enzyme expression. Avoid bottlenecks, toxicity. Cybernetic control for optimal production.
Explain how fossil completeness affects dating | evolution | Fossil completeness: more complete fossils easier to place phylogenetically, reduce uncertainty. Incomplete fossils still useful with careful morphological analysis.
What is a human-pig chimera for liver disease? | research | Human hepatocytes in pig liver model liver diseases, test drugs. Pigs similar liver size, physiology. Challenges: human cell engraftment, immune rejection.
How does histone variant H2A.Z affect genes? | epigenetics | H2A.Z: deposited at promoters, nucleosome destabilizing, ambiguous role in transcription (activates or represses depending on context). Involved in memory, stress response.
What is a synteny for sex chromosome evolution? | research | Sex chromosome evolution: synteny between X/Y or Z/W shows degeneration, loss of recombination, accumulation of repeats. Compare across species with different sex determination.
Explain how promoter escape is regulated | processes | Promoter escape regulated by: initiation factor phosphorylation, mediator, nucleosome positioning, DNA sequence (consensus at +1). Rate-limiting step for some genes.
What is a genetic marker for pollinator health? | applications | Pollinator health genetics: pesticide resistance, disease susceptibility, foraging behavior. Breeding resilient honeybees, conserving wild pollinators.
How does hard sweep signature appear? | evolution | Hard sweep signature: extended haplotype homozygosity, reduced diversity, skewed site frequency spectrum, increased linkage disequilibrium around selected site.
What is a ribozyme for RNA sequencing library prep? | research | RNA-seq library prep: ribozymes cleave RNA to generate uniform ends, reduce bias. Alternative to enzymatic fragmentation, more controlled.
Explain how imprinting affects metabolic syndrome | disorders | Imprinting and metabolic syndrome: Prader-Willi obesity, Temple syndrome insulin resistance, transient neonatal diabetes. Imprinted genes in hypothalamus, pancreas, adipose.
What is a haplotype for cancer immunotherapy? | genetics | Cancer immunotherapy haplotypes: HLA for neoantigen presentation; immune checkpoint gene haplotypes (PD-L1, CTLA-4); cytokine haplotypes. Predict response, toxicity.
How does CRISPR screen identify synthetic rescue? | research | Synthetic rescue screen: knockout library in disease background, look for suppressors of phenotype. Identify compensatory pathways, potential therapeutic targets.
What is a genetic algorithm for aerodynamic design? | applications | Aerodynamic design: evolve wing, airfoil shapes for optimal lift, drag. Used in aircraft, automotive, turbine design. Unconventional solutions.
Explain how Hox genes pattern the nervous system | genetics | Hox genes pattern nervous system: specify motor neuron pools in spinal cord; regional identity in hindbrain; axon guidance. Disrupted in neurodevelopmental disorders.
What is a protoplast for membrane protein studies? | research | Membrane protein studies: protoplasts for localization, trafficking, activity assays of channels, transporters. Easier than whole cells for some assays.
How does genomic imprinting affect livestock breeding? | genetics | Livestock imprinting: affects growth, carcass traits. Use in breeding: select based on parent-of-origin. Examples: callipyge sheep, IGF2 in pigs.
What is a genetic correlation with COVID-19 severity? | research | COVID-19 severity genetics: HLA, blood type, interferon pathway genes. Correlates with autoimmune, inflammatory traits. Polygenic risk scores predict severe outcomes.
Explain how vaccine platforms induce different immunity | technology | Immunity differences: mRNA strong neutralizing antibodies, CD8 T cells; viral vector strong CD8 T cells; protein subunit mainly antibodies. Choice depends on pathogen.
What is a morphogen in tooth regeneration? | genetics | Tooth regeneration morphogens: BMP, FGF, Wnt stimulate tooth formation from stem cells. Bioengineered teeth, enamel regeneration. Dental tissue engineering.
How does spatial transcriptomics guide surgery? | technology | Surgical guidance: spatial transcriptomics on biopsy margins identify residual tumor, guide resection. Real-time during surgery with rapid protocols.
What is a genetic network for antibiotic production? | research | Antibiotic production network: pathway genes, regulators, resistance genes. Engineering for new antibiotics, increased yield. Combat antibiotic resistance.
Explain how speciation reversal occurs | evolution | Speciation reversal: hybrid swarms merge previously distinct species due to human disturbance, climate change. Loss of biodiversity, homogeneization.
What is a degron for protein degradation in plants? | research | Plant degron systems: auxin-inducible, gibberellin-inducible. Study gene function, control transgene expression. Agricultural biotechnology applications.
How does transcription factor phase separation work? | genetics | Phase separation: intrinsically disordered regions mediate liquid-liquid phase separation, concentrate transcription factors, coactivators at super-enhancers. Regulates transcription bursting.
What is a genetic switch for orthogonal control? | engineering | Orthogonal genetic switches: respond to synthetic inducers not found in nature (plant hormones in bacteria, etc.). Prevent crosstalk, enable independent control of multiple pathways.
Explain how molecular dating estimates uncertainty | evolution | Bayesian dating estimates uncertainty: posterior probability distributions for node ages, credibility intervals. Incorporates fossil uncertainty, model uncertainty, sequence uncertainty.
What is a human-mouse chimera for aging research? | research | Heterochronic parabiosis: young blood effects on old tissues studied in chimeras. Aging mechanisms, rejuvenation factors. Controversial but active area.
How does histone acetylation affect memory formation? | epigenetics | Histone acetylation in memory: increased at memory-related gene promoters during learning, regulated by HATs (CBP), HDACs. Epigenetic basis of long-term memory.
What is a synteny for polyploid hybrid vigor? | research | Heterosis in polyploids: synteny helps understand allelic interactions between subgenomes, dosage effects. Molecular basis of hybrid vigor in crops like maize.
Explain how intrinsic termination is efficient | processes | Intrinsic termination efficiency near 100% for strong terminators. Hairpin stability and U-stretch crucial. Engineered terminators for synthetic biology often >95% efficient.
What is a genetic marker for assisted evolution? | applications | Assisted evolution: identify heat-tolerant corals, drought-tolerant trees, etc. for selective breeding, assisted migration. Climate change adaptation.
How does background selection affect linked sites? | evolution | Background selection: reduces effective population size for linked neutral sites, increasing drift, reducing diversity. Effect extends several kilobases from selected site.
What is a ribozyme for RNA imaging in live cells? | research | Live-cell RNA imaging: self-cleaving ribozymes generate ends for ligation of fluorescent probes inside cells. Real-time RNA tracking, localization dynamics.
Explain how imprinting affects fetal development | disorders | Imprinting crucial for fetal development: growth regulation, placental function, organ development. Errors cause syndromes with multi-system effects, often growth-related.
What is a haplotype for rare disease diagnosis? | genetics | Rare disease diagnosis: identify haplotypes shared by affected individuals in families, pinpoint causal variants. Autozygosity mapping in consanguineous families.
How does CRISPR screen map enhancer networks? | research | Enhancer network mapping: CRISPRi/a across many enhancers with single-cell RNA-seq reveals interconnected regulatory landscapes, hierarchy, redundancy.
What is a genetic algorithm for financial forecasting? | applications | Financial forecasting: evolve trading rules, indicators. Combine technical analysis, machine learning. Adaptive to market regimes, but risk of overfitting.
Explain how Hox genes regulate limb patterning | genetics | Hox genes in limb: specify proximal-distal identity; interact with SHH for anterior-posterior; with Wnt for dorsal-ventral. Coordinated regulation of growth, patterning.
What is a protoplast for synthetic chloroplasts? | research | Synthetic chloroplasts: introduce engineered genomes into protoplasts, regenerate plants with modified photosynthesis. Solar-to-fuel, enhanced carbon fixation.
How does parent-of-origin effect affect hybrid vigor? | genetics | Heterosis: parent-of-origin effects may contribute to hybrid vigor. Differential expression of imprinted genes in hybrids, optimal combinations.
What is a genetic correlation with vaccination response? | research | Vaccination response genetics: antibody levels, cell-mediated response heritable. Correlates with immune traits, age. Personalize vaccine schedules, adjuvants.
Explain how vaccine platforms address variants | technology | Variant-proof vaccines: mRNA easily updated to match new variants; viral vector can be modified; protein subunit may need redesign. Platform flexibility important for pandemics.
What is a morphogen in bone remodeling? | genetics | Bone remodeling morphogens: RANKL/OPG balance regulates osteoclasts; Wnt, BMP regulate osteoblasts. Therapeutic for osteoporosis, bone defects.
How does single-cell epigenomics reveal disease states? | technology | Disease epigenomics: chromatin accessibility changes in autoimmune disease, cancer, neurodegeneration. Identify dysregulated enhancers, cell states driving pathology.
What is a genetic network for nitrogen use efficiency? | research | Nitrogen use efficiency network: uptake, assimilation, signaling genes. Engineering for reduced fertilizer use, sustainable agriculture. Key for food security.
Explain how sensory drive influences speciation | evolution | Sensory drive: adaptation of sensory systems to environment affects mate choice, leading to speciation. Example: cichlid fish color vision and coloration.
What is a light-activated Cre for lineage tracing? | research | Photoactivatable Cre: CreER with photocaged tamoxifen; or split Cre with light-induced dimerization. Precise spatial-temporal lineage tracing in development.
How does alternative end joining work? | processes | Alternative end joining: uses microhomology, involves PARP1, Lig3, often deletional. Backup pathway when NHEJ, HR impaired. Contributes to genome instability.
What is a genetic switch for minimal metabolism? | engineering | Minimal metabolism: essential pathways under inducible control, study core metabolism. Synthetic minimal cells for basic biology, biotechnology.
Explain how fossil record completeness affects dating | evolution | Fossil record completeness: estimated from sedimentary rock volume, preservation potential. Models incorporate completeness to correct divergence time estimates.
What is a human-pig chimera for heart disease? | research | Human cardiomyocytes in pig heart model arrhythmias, test drugs. Challenges: electrical integration, immune rejection. Xenotransplantation for heart failure.
How does histone lactylation affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone lactylation: links metabolism to transcription, marks active genes in macrophages after lactate accumulation. New modification, functions emerging.
What is a synteny for domestication genomics? | research | Domestication genomics: synteny between crops and wild relatives identifies selected regions, causal genes. Understand domestication syndrome, accelerate breeding.
Explain how promoter escape kinetics vary | processes | Promoter escape kinetics: fast for some genes (immediate early), slow for others (highly regulated). Affects response dynamics, noise, regulatory strategies.
What is a genetic marker for bee breeding? | applications | Bee breeding: disease resistance (Varroa), hygienic behavior, honey production markers. Genomic selection for healthier bees, pollination efficiency.
How does selective sweep affect linked variation? | evolution | Selective sweep: reduces diversity, increases linkage disequilibrium around selected site. Hard sweep affects larger region than soft sweep. Signature used to detect selection.
What is a ribozyme for RNA circularization in cells? | research | Circular RNA production: self-splicing introns produce circRNAs naturally; engineered for stable expression. Functions: miRNA sponge, protein scaffold, translation.
Explain how imprinting affects adult metabolism | disorders | Imprinting affects adult metabolism beyond syndromes: common variants near imprinted loci associated with BMI, glucose, lipids. Lifelong effects from fetal programming.
What is a haplotype for transplant rejection risk? | genetics | Transplant rejection: HLA matching primary, also minor histocompatibility antigen haplotypes, KIR haplotypes. Non-HLA antibodies also important.
How does CRISPR screen identify disease modifiers? | research | Disease modifier screens: in disease model (e.g., neurodegenerative protein aggregation), CRISPR screen identifies genes that enhance or suppress phenotype. Therapeutic targets.
What is a genetic algorithm for materials discovery? | applications | Materials discovery: evolve chemical compositions, crystal structures for desired properties (strength, conductivity, catalysis). Accelerate materials innovation.
Explain how Hox genes are involved in cancer metastasis | genetics | Hox genes in metastasis: some promote (HOXA10 in endometrial cancer), others suppress (HOXA5 in breast). Regulate adhesion, invasion, stemness. Context-dependent.
What is a protoplast for genome imaging? | research | Genome imaging in protoplasts: easier for DNA FISH, live imaging of chromatin. Study nuclear organization, chromosome dynamics in plants.
How does genomic imprinting affect plant breeding? | genetics | Plant imprinting: affects seed size, endosperm development. Use in breeding hybrid crops. Different from mammals, mainly in endosperm.
What is a genetic correlation with microbiome composition? | research | Host genetics-microbiome: immune genes, diet-related genes influence microbiome. Mendelian randomization suggests bidirectional effects on health traits.
Explain how mRNA vaccine safety was established | technology | mRNA vaccine safety: decades of research, lipid nanoparticle optimization, purity, rigorous trials. Rare side effects (myocarditis) identified, risk-benefit favorable.
What is a morphogen in cartilage development? | genetics | Cartilage development morphogens: TGF-β, BMP induce chondrogenesis; Wnt, FGF regulate hypertrophy; Ihh regulates growth plate. Tissue engineering for arthritis.
How does spatial transcriptomics map tumor margins? | technology | Tumor margin mapping: spatial transcriptomics distinguishes tumor, stroma, immune cells at single-cell resolution. Guide precise resection, spare healthy tissue.
What is a genetic network for carbon fixation? | research | Carbon fixation network: Rubisco, Calvin cycle, photorespiration. Engineering C4 into C3 plants, synthetic pathways (CETCH cycle). Climate change mitigation.
Explain how speciation genes are identified | evolution | Speciation genes: cause hybrid incompatibility (Dobzhansky-Muller incompatibilities). Identified by crosses, introgression mapping, gene expression in hybrids.
What is a temperature-sensitive cell cycle mutant? | research | Cell cycle ts mutants: arrest at specific phase at restrictive temperature. Classic in yeast (cdc mutants). Study cell cycle controls, checkpoints.
How does transcription factor dosage sensitivity arise? | genetics | Dosage sensitivity: haploinsufficiency when 50% protein not enough; triplosensitivity when 150% too much. Due to stoichiometry, network properties.
What is a genetic switch for biofilm control? | engineering | Biofilm control: induce dispersal enzymes, kill switch activated by quorum sensing. Prevent biofouling, treat chronic infections.
Explain how molecular dating uses multiple genes | evolution | Multiple gene dating: concatenated or species tree methods account for gene tree discordance. Coalescent-based species tree estimation reduces error from incomplete lineage sorting.
What is a human-mouse chimera for muscle disease? | research | Human muscle stem cells in mouse model muscular dystrophy, test therapies. Challenges: engraftment, functional integration, immune rejection.
How does histone methylation affect aging? | epigenetics | Aging epigenetics: H3K4me3 increases, H3K9me3 decreases in some contexts. Epigenetic clocks based on DNA methylation predict age, mortality.
What is a synteny for evolutionary developmental biology? | research | Evo-devo synteny: compare regulatory landscapes of developmental genes across species. Understand evolution of body plans, regulatory innovation.
Explain how intrinsic termination is modulated | processes | Intrinsic termination modulated by: RNA polymerase mutations, transcription factors, nucleotides (GTP concentration), topological stress. Natural variation in efficiency.
What is a genetic marker for seed banking? | applications | Seed banking genetics: assess diversity, inbreeding, adaptation. Guide collection strategies, regeneration intervals. Conserve crop wild relatives.
How does background selection affect Fst? | evolution | Background selection reduces within-population diversity, can increase Fst between populations at linked sites even without differential selection.
What is a ribozyme for therapeutic RNA delivery? | applications | Therapeutic RNA delivery: ribozymes cleave to release active RNA from carrier. Improve pharmacokinetics, tissue-specific activation. In development.
Explain how imprinting affects neurodevelopmental disorders | disorders | Neurodevelopmental disorders: Prader-Willi, Angelman, Temple syndromes. Imprinted genes crucial for brain development, synaptic function, behavior.
What is a haplotype for complex disease risk? | genetics | Complex disease haplotypes: combinations of SNPs in LD often better predictors than single SNPs. Capture epistasis, rare variants on same haplotype.
How does CRISPR screen identify synthetic sick interactions? | research | Synthetic sick: combining two knockouts worse than additive. Map genetic interaction networks, pathway relationships, drug combinations.
What is a genetic algorithm for supply chain optimization? | applications | Supply chain optimization: evolve logistics networks, inventory management, demand forecasting. Complex constraints, dynamic environments.
Explain how Hox genes regulate segmentation | genetics | Hox genes regulate segmentation: specify identity of segments after they are formed by segmentation genes. Coordinate with clock-and-wavefront in somitogenesis.
What is a protoplast for rapid trait testing? | research | Rapid trait testing: protoplast assays for stress tolerance, herbicide resistance, metabolic engineering. High-throughput before whole plant studies.
How does parent-of-origin effect affect genomic selection? | genetics | Genomic selection accounting for imprinting: separate breeding values for maternal and paternal alleles. Improve accuracy for traits with imprinting.
What is a genetic correlation with telomere length? | research | Telomere length genetics: associated with aging, cancer, cardiovascular disease. Polygenic scores predict length, but environmental factors substantial.
Explain how vaccine platforms are stored/distributed | technology | Vaccine storage/distribution: mRNA ultra-cold initially, now refrigerated; viral vector refrigerated; protein subunit refrigerated; live attenuated often frozen. Cold chain critical.
What is a morphogen in hair regeneration? | genetics | Hair regeneration morphogens: Wnt activates stem cells, BMP inhibits, FGF promotes growth. Therapeutic for alopecia, wound healing.
How does single-cell epigenomics capture heterogeneity? | technology | Cellular heterogeneity: epigenomics reveals distinct regulatory states within seemingly uniform cell populations. Cancer subclones, immune cell states, neuronal diversity.
What is a genetic network for drought tolerance? | research | Drought tolerance network: ABA signaling, stomatal regulation, root architecture, osmotic adjustment. Engineering crops for water-limited environments.
Explain how parallel speciation occurs | evolution | Parallel speciation: similar environments drive independent evolution of reproductive isolation in different populations. Example: stickleback freshwater adaptation.
What is a light-activated Cas13 for RNA control? | research | Optogenetic Cas13: control RNA targeting, degradation with light. Spatial-temporal RNA regulation, study RNA dynamics, therapeutic applications.
How does single-strand annealing repair work? | processes | Single-strand annealing: resection reveals complementary repeats, anneal, flap removal, ligation. Deletional, uses Rad52. Important in some genome editing outcomes.
What is a genetic switch for programmed death? | engineering | Programmed cell death switches: toxin genes under control of population density, environmental signals. Containment, therapy (suicide genes in cancer).
Explain how fossil dating methods are combined | evolution | Combined dating: radiometric (U-Pb, Ar-Ar), biostratigraphy, magnetostratigraphy, cyclostratigraphy. Cross-validation improves accuracy, reduces uncertainty.
What is a human-pig chimera for kidney disease? | research | Human nephrons in pig kidney model renal disease, test drugs. Pigs similar kidney physiology. Xenotransplantation for kidney failure.
How does histone crotonylation affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone crotonylation: marks active promoters, enhancers. Regulated by crotonyl-CoA availability. Links metabolism to transcription, spermatogenesis.
What is a synteny for paleogenomics? | research | Paleogenomics: align ancient DNA to modern reference genomes using synteny, despite fragmentation. Study extinct species, past populations.
Explain how promoter clearance is rate-limiting | processes | Promoter clearance rate-limiting for some genes: regulated by factors, nucleosomes. Affects transcriptional bursting frequency, noise, response dynamics.
What is a genetic marker for forest restoration? | applications | Forest restoration genetics: source appropriate genotypes, maintain diversity, assist migration. Climate-smart reforestation, ecosystem services.
How does hitchhiking affect neutral tests? | evolution | Hitchhiking affects neutrality tests (Tajima's D, Fay & Wu's H). Distinguishing selection from demography challenging, need multiple lines of evidence.
What is a ribozyme for RNA purification? | research | RNA purification: affinity tags inserted via ribozyme cleavage sites. Purify RNA-protein complexes, study RNPs, therapeutic RNA production.
Explain how imprinting affects growth hormone axis | disorders | Imprinting and growth: GNAS complex locus imprinted, involved in growth hormone signaling. Mutations cause pseudohypoparathyroidism, growth abnormalities.
What is a haplotype for autoimmune disease risk? | genetics | Autoimmune disease haplotypes: HLA haplotypes major risk (DR4 for rheumatoid arthritis, DR3-DQ2 for celiac). Non-HLA haplotypes also important.
How does CRISPR screen identify enhancer function? | research | Enhancer function screens: tiling deletion with CRISPR, measure effects on gene expression, chromatin. High-resolution mapping of regulatory elements.
What is a genetic algorithm for antenna optimization? | applications | Antenna optimization: evolve shapes for specific frequency, gain, bandwidth. Used in telecommunications, satellite, radar systems.
Explain how Hox genes are regulated by retinoic acid in development | genetics | Retinoic acid regulates Hox genes: gradients established by synthesis (RALDH) and degradation (CYP26), posteriorizing signal. Used experimentally to alter Hox expression.
What is a protoplast for chloroplast transformation? | research | Chloroplast transformation: deliver DNA to protoplasts, regenerate, select for chloroplast-encoded traits. High expression, maternal inheritance, containment.
How does genomic imprinting affect human evolution? | evolution | Human imprinting evolution: possibly involved in brain evolution, social behavior. Comparative genomics with primates shows conserved and human-specific imprinting.
What is a genetic correlation with brain structure? | research | Brain structure genetics: cortical thickness, volume heritable. Correlates with cognitive abilities, psychiatric disorders. Imaging genetics large consortia.
Explain how vaccine platforms address equity | technology | Vaccine equity: mRNA scalable but cold chain; viral vector single dose but pre-existing immunity; protein subunit stable but weaker immunity. Platform choice affects global access.
What is a morphogen in synovial joint formation? | genetics | Joint formation morphogens: GDF5 specifies joint location; Wnt, BMP regulate interzone formation; Ihh regulates growth. Osteoarthritis research.
How does spatial transcriptomics map development? | technology | Developmental mapping: spatial transcriptomics captures gene expression patterns in embryos, organogenesis. Create atlases, study patterning, cell fate decisions.
What is a genetic network for phosphate uptake? | research | Phosphate uptake network: transporters, signaling (PHR, SPX), root architecture. Engineering crops for low-phosphate soils, reduce fertilizer.
Explain how ecological character displacement occurs | evolution | Ecological character displacement: competition drives divergence in resource use, morphology. Reduces competition, can lead to speciation. Classic example: Galapagos finches.
What is a light-activated split Cre system? | research | Split Cre with light dimerization: fragments fused to photodimerizable domains, reconstitute with light. Reduce leakiness, improve spatial control.
How does transcription factor binding kinetics matter? | genetics | Binding kinetics: on/off rates affect response time, noise filtering, memory. Measured by SPR, EMSA, single-molecule methods. Engineered for synthetic biology.
What is a genetic switch for orthogonal replication? | engineering | Orthogonal replication: synthetic origin of replication, polymerase for containment. Engineered chromosomes, synthetic life forms.
Explain how molecular dating handles missing data | evolution | Missing data handling: models account for incomplete sampling (fossils, genes). Bayesian methods integrate over uncertain placements, ages.
What is a human-mouse chimera for liver regeneration? | research | Human hepatocytes in mouse liver model regeneration, test pro-regenerative drugs. Partial hepatectomy, injury models.
How does histone benzoylation affect transcription? | epigenetics | Histone benzoylation: newly discovered, function unclear. Links metabolism (benzoyl-CoA) to chromatin. Rapidly expanding list of modifications.
What is a synteny for crop domestication? | research | Crop domestication synteny: compare crops to wild relatives, identify selected haplotypes. Accelerate de novo domestication of wild species.
Explain how promoter escape involves TFIIH | processes | TFIIH in promoter escape: helicase unwinds DNA, kinase (CDK7) phosphorylates Pol II CTD. Mutations cause xeroderma pigmentosum, trichothiodystrophy.

How does selective sweep affect site frequency spectrum? | evolution | Selective sweep skews site frequency spectrum: excess of rare variants (positive selection) or intermediate frequencies (balancing selection). Tajima's D detects.
